<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hamburgisch_dialect" title="Hamburgisch dialect">Hamburgisch dialect</a></div>
<p>Like elsewhere in Germany, <a href="/wiki/Standard_German" title="Standard German">Standard German</a> is spoken in Hamburg, but as typical for northern Germany, the original language of Hamburg is <a href="/wiki/Low_German" title="Low German">Low German</a>, usually referred to as <i>Hamborger Platt</i> (German <i>Hamburger Platt</i>) or <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburgisch" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburgisch">Hamborgsch</a></i>. Since large-scale <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">standardization</a> of the German language beginning in earnest in the 18th century, various Low German-colored dialects have developed (contact-varieties of German on Low Saxon substrates). Originally, there was a range of such <a href="/wiki/Missingsch" title="Missingsch">Missingsch</a> varieties, the best-known being the low-prestige ones of the working classes and the somewhat more bourgeois <i>Hanseatendeutsch</i> (Hanseatic German), although the term is used in appreciation.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> All of these are now moribund due to the influences of Standard German used by education and media. However, the former importance of Low German is indicated by several songs, such as the famous <a href="/wiki/Sea_shanty" title="Sea shanty">sea shanty</a> <a href="/wiki/Hamborger_Veermaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamborger Veermaster">Hamborger Veermaster</a>, written in the 19th century when Low German was used more frequently. Many toponyms and street names reflect Low Saxon vocabulary, partially even in Low Saxon spelling, which is not standardised, and to some part in forms adapted to Standard German.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Slightly less than half of the residents of Hamburg are members of a religion. In late 2015, 27.0% of the population belonged to the <a href="/wiki/North_Elbian_Evangelical_Lutheran_Church" title="North Elbian Evangelical Lutheran Church">North Elbian Evangelical Lutheran Church</a>, the largest religious body, and 10.7% to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> An additional 55% stated they had no religion.</p>
<p>According to the publication "Muslimisches Leben in Deutschland" estimated 141,900 Muslim migrants (counting in nearly 50 countries of origin) lived in Hamburg in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> About three years later (May 2011) calculations based on census data for 21 countries of origin resulted in the number of about 143,200 Muslim migrants in Hamburg, making up 8.4% percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamburg is seat of one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_bishops_of_Hamburg#Bishops_of_Hamburg_and_L.C3.BCbeck_.28as_of_2008.29" title="List of bishops of Hamburg">three</a> bishops of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_Northern_Germany" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in Northern Germany">Evangelical Lutheran Church in Northern Germany</a> and seat of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Hamburg" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Hamburg">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Hamburg</a>. There are several mosques, including the <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> run <a href="/wiki/Fazle_Omar_Mosque" title="Fazle Omar Mosque">Fazle Omar Mosque</a>, which is the oldest in the city,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Centre_Hamburg" title="Islamic Centre Hamburg">Islamic Centre Hamburg</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Hamburg" title="Government of Hamburg">Government of Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Hamburg" title="List of mayors of Hamburg">List of mayors of Hamburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG/170px-Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG/255px-Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG/340px-Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2533" data-file-height="3823" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_town_hall_tower.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hamburg City Hall (front view)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city of Hamburg is one of 16 <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">German states</a>, therefore the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Hamburg" title="Government of Hamburg">Mayor of Hamburg</a>'s office corresponds more to the role of a <a href="/wiki/Minister-president" title="Minister-president">minister-president</a> than to the one of a city mayor. As a <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany#Politics" title="States of Germany">German state government</a>, it is responsible for public education, correctional institutions and public safety; as a municipality, it is additionally responsible for libraries, recreational facilities, sanitation, water supply and welfare services.</p>
<p>Since 1897, the seat of the government has been the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Rathaus" title="Hamburg Rathaus">Hamburg Rathaus</a>, with the office of the mayor, the meeting room for the Senate and the floor for the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Parliament" title="Hamburg Parliament">Hamburg Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rathaus_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rathaus-46">[45]</a></sup> From 2001 until 2010, the mayor of Hamburg was <a href="/wiki/Ole_von_Beust" title="Ole von Beust">Ole von Beust</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-usatoday2008_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday2008-47">[46]</a></sup> who governed in Germany's first statewide "black-green" coalition, consisting of the conservative <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">CDU</a> and the alternative GAL, which are Hamburg's regional wing of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a> party.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Von Beust was briefly succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Ahlhaus" title="Christoph Ahlhaus">Christoph Ahlhaus</a> in 2010, but the coalition broke apart on November, 28. 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> On 7 March 2011 <a href="/wiki/Olaf_Scholz" title="Olaf Scholz">Olaf Scholz</a> (SPD) became mayor.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs">Boroughs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Boroughs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_and_quarters_of_Hamburg" title="Boroughs and quarters of Hamburg">Boroughs and quarters of Hamburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg/250px-Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg.png" width="250" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg/375px-Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg/500px-Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1713" data-file-height="1689" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_Subdivisions.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 7 boroughs and 104 quarters of Hamburg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamburg is made up of seven boroughs (German: <i>Bezirke</i>) and subdivided into 104 quarters (German: <i>Stadtteile</i>). There are 181 localities (German: <i>Ortsteile</i>). The urban organization is regulated by the Constitution of Hamburg and several laws.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-6">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-borough_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borough-50">[49]</a></sup> Most of the quarters were former independent cities, towns or villages annexed into Hamburg proper. The last large annexation was done through the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Hamburg_Act" title="Greater Hamburg Act">Greater Hamburg Act</a> of 1937, when the cities <a href="/wiki/Altona,_Hamburg" title="Altona, Hamburg">Altona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harburg,_Hamburg" title="Harburg, Hamburg">Harburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Wandsbek" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Wandsbek">Wandsbek</a> were merged into the state of Hamburg.<sup id="cite_ref-greateract_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greateract-51">[50]</a></sup> The <i>Act of the Constitution and Administration of Hanseatic city of Hamburg</i> established Hamburg as a state and a municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-reichconst_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reichconst-52">[51]</a></sup> Some of the boroughs and quarters have been rearranged several times.</p>
<p>Each borough is governed by a Borough Council (German: <i>Bezirksversammlung</i>) and administered by a Municipal Administrator (German: <i>Bezirksamtsleiter</i>). The boroughs are not independent municipalities: their power is limited and subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Hamburg">Senate of Hamburg</a>. The borough administrator is elected by the Borough Council and thereafter requires confirmation and appointment by Hamburg's Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-borough_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-borough-50">[49]</a></sup> The quarters have no governing bodies of their own.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Germany_(2),_Neuwerk,_Scharh%C3%B6rn,_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Germany_%282%29%2C_Neuwerk%2C_Scharh%C3%B6rn%2C_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg/220px-Germany_%282%29%2C_Neuwerk%2C_Scharh%C3%B6rn%2C_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Germany_%282%29%2C_Neuwerk%2C_Scharh%C3%B6rn%2C_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg/330px-Germany_%282%29%2C_Neuwerk%2C_Scharh%C3%B6rn%2C_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Germany_%282%29%2C_Neuwerk%2C_Scharh%C3%B6rn%2C_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg/440px-Germany_%282%29%2C_Neuwerk%2C_Scharh%C3%B6rn%2C_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1941" data-file-height="1684" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Germany_(2),_Neuwerk,_Scharh%C3%B6rn,_Nigeh%C3%B6rn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The part of the North Sea in this aerial picture is called the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Wadden_Sea_National_Park" title="Hamburg Wadden Sea National Park">Hamburg Wadden Sea National Park</a> and belongs administratively to the borough of <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Mitte" title="Hamburg-Mitte">Hamburg-Mitte</a>. Some 39 people live here on the island <a href="/wiki/Neuwerk" title="Neuwerk">Neuwerk</a> (visible just above the centre).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2008, the boroughs were <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Mitte" title="Hamburg-Mitte">Hamburg-Mitte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altona,_Hamburg" title="Altona, Hamburg">Altona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eimsb%C3%BCttel" title="Eimsbüttel">Eimsbüttel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Nord" title="Hamburg-Nord">Hamburg-Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wandsbek" title="Wandsbek">Wandsbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bergedorf" title="Bergedorf">Bergedorf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harburg,_Hamburg" title="Harburg, Hamburg">Harburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Mitte" title="Hamburg-Mitte">Hamburg-Mitte</a></i> ("Hamburg Centre") covers mostly the urban centre of the city and consists of the quarters <a href="/wiki/Billbrook" title="Billbrook">Billbrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billstedt" title="Billstedt">Billstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borgfelde" title="Borgfelde">Borgfelde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finkenwerder" title="Finkenwerder">Finkenwerder</a>, <a href="/wiki/HafenCity" title="HafenCity">HafenCity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamm,_Hamburg" title="Hamm, Hamburg">Hamm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hammerbrook" title="Hammerbrook">Hammerbrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horn,_Hamburg" title="Horn, Hamburg">Horn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kleiner_Grasbrook" title="Kleiner Grasbrook">Kleiner Grasbrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuwerk" title="Neuwerk">Neuwerk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rothenburgsort" title="Rothenburgsort">Rothenburgsort</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Georg,_Hamburg" title="St. Georg, Hamburg">St. Georg</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Pauli" title="St. Pauli">St. Pauli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steinwerder" class="mw-redirect" title="Steinwerder">Steinwerder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veddel" title="Veddel">Veddel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waltershof" title="Waltershof">Waltershof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmsburg,_Hamburg" title="Wilhelmsburg, Hamburg">Wilhelmsburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup> The quarters <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altstadt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Altstadt">Hamburg-Altstadt</a> ("old town") and <a href="/wiki/Neustadt,_Hamburg" title="Neustadt, Hamburg">Neustadt</a> ("new town") are the historical origin of Hamburg.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Altona,_Hamburg" title="Altona, Hamburg">Altona</a></i> is the westernmost urban borough, on the right bank of the Elbe river. From 1640 to 1864, Altona was under the administration of the Danish monarchy. Altona was an independent city until 1937. Politically, the following quarters are part of Altona: <a href="/wiki/Altona-Altstadt" title="Altona-Altstadt">Altona-Altstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altona-Nord" title="Altona-Nord">Altona-Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrenfeld" title="Bahrenfeld">Bahrenfeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottensen" title="Ottensen">Ottensen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Othmarschen" title="Othmarschen">Othmarschen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9F_Flottbek" title="Groß Flottbek">Groß Flottbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osdorf,_Hamburg" title="Osdorf, Hamburg">Osdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lurup" title="Lurup">Lurup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nienstedten" title="Nienstedten">Nienstedten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blankenese" title="Blankenese">Blankenese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iserbrook" title="Iserbrook">Iserbrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BClldorf" title="Sülldorf">Sülldorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rissen" title="Rissen">Rissen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sternschanze" title="Sternschanze">Sternschanze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Bergedorf" title="Bergedorf">Bergedorf</a></i> consists of the quarters <a href="/wiki/Allerm%C3%B6he" title="Allermöhe">Allermöhe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Altengamme" title="Altengamme">Altengamme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bergedorf_(quarter)" title="Bergedorf (quarter)">Bergedorf</a>—the centre of the former independent town, <a href="/wiki/Billwerder" title="Billwerder">Billwerder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curslack" title="Curslack">Curslack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kirchwerder" title="Kirchwerder">Kirchwerder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lohbr%C3%BCgge" title="Lohbrügge">Lohbrügge</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moorfleet&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Moorfleet (page does not exist)">Moorfleet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuengamme" title="Neuengamme">Neuengamme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuallerm%C3%B6he" title="Neuallermöhe">Neuallermöhe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ochsenwerder" title="Ochsenwerder">Ochsenwerder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reitbrook" title="Reitbrook">Reitbrook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spadenland" title="Spadenland">Spadenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tatenberg" title="Tatenberg">Tatenberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Eimsb%C3%BCttel" title="Eimsbüttel">Eimsbüttel</a></i> is split into nine quarters: <a href="/wiki/Eidelstedt" title="Eidelstedt">Eidelstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eimsb%C3%BCttel_(quarter)" title="Eimsbüttel (quarter)">Eimsbüttel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harvestehude" title="Harvestehude">Harvestehude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoheluft-West" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoheluft-West">Hoheluft-West</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lokstedt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lokstedt (page does not exist)">Lokstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niendorf,_Hamburg" title="Niendorf, Hamburg">Niendorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotherbaum" title="Rotherbaum">Rotherbaum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schnelsen" title="Schnelsen">Schnelsen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stellingen" class="mw-redirect" title="Stellingen">Stellingen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup> Located within this borough is former Jewish neighbourhood Grindel.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Nord" title="Hamburg-Nord">Hamburg-Nord</a></i> contains the quarters <a href="/wiki/Alsterdorf" title="Alsterdorf">Alsterdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barmbek-Nord" title="Barmbek-Nord">Barmbek-Nord</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barmbek-S%C3%BCd" title="Barmbek-Süd">Barmbek-Süd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dulsberg" title="Dulsberg">Dulsberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eppendorf,_Hamburg" title="Eppendorf, Hamburg">Eppendorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuhlsb%C3%BCttel" title="Fuhlsbüttel">Fuhlsbüttel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gro%C3%9F_Borstel" title="Groß Borstel">Groß Borstel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoheluft-Ost" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoheluft-Ost">Hoheluft-Ost</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hohenfelde,_Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hohenfelde, Hamburg (page does not exist)">Hohenfelde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Langenhorn,_Hamburg" title="Langenhorn, Hamburg">Langenhorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohlsdorf" title="Ohlsdorf">Ohlsdorf</a> with <a href="/wiki/Friedhof_Ohlsdorf" class="mw-redirect" title="Friedhof Ohlsdorf">Ohlsdorf cemetery</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Uhlenhorst&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Uhlenhorst (page does not exist)">Uhlenhorst</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winterhude" title="Winterhude">Winterhude</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Harburg,_Hamburg" title="Harburg, Hamburg">Harburg</a></i> lies on the southern shores of the river Elbe and covers parts of the port of Hamburg, residential and rural areas, and some research institutes. The quarters are <a href="/wiki/Altenwerder" title="Altenwerder">Altenwerder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cranz,_Hamburg" title="Cranz, Hamburg">Cranz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ei%C3%9Fendorf" title="Eißendorf">Eißendorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francop" title="Francop">Francop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gut_Moor" title="Gut Moor">Gut Moor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harburg_(quarter)" title="Harburg (quarter)">Harburg</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hausbruch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hausbruch (page does not exist)">Hausbruch</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heimfeld&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Heimfeld (page does not exist)">Heimfeld</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Langenbek&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Langenbek (page does not exist)">Langenbek</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marmstorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marmstorf (page does not exist)">Marmstorf</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moorburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Moorburg (page does not exist)">Moorburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuenfelde" title="Neuenfelde">Neuenfelde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neugraben-Fischbek" title="Neugraben-Fischbek">Neugraben-Fischbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuland,_Hamburg" title="Neuland, Hamburg">Neuland</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=R%C3%B6nneburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rönneburg (page does not exist)">Rönneburg</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sinstorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sinstorf (page does not exist)">Sinstorf</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilstorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wilstorf (page does not exist)">Wilstorf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Wandsbek" title="Wandsbek">Wandsbek</a></i> is divided into the quarters <a href="/wiki/Bergstedt" title="Bergstedt">Bergstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bramfeld" title="Bramfeld">Bramfeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duvenstedt" title="Duvenstedt">Duvenstedt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eilbek" title="Eilbek">Eilbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farmsen-Berne" title="Farmsen-Berne">Farmsen-Berne</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hummelsb%C3%BCttel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hummelsbüttel (page does not exist)">Hummelsbüttel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jenfeld&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jenfeld (page does not exist)">Jenfeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemsahl-Mellingstedt" title="Lemsahl-Mellingstedt">Lemsahl-Mellingstedt</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marienthal,_Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marienthal, Hamburg (page does not exist)">Marienthal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poppenb%C3%BCttel" title="Poppenbüttel">Poppenbüttel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rahlstedt" title="Rahlstedt">Rahlstedt</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sasel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sasel (page does not exist)">Sasel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Steilshoop&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Steilshoop (page does not exist)">Steilshoop</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tonndorf,_Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tonndorf, Hamburg (page does not exist)">Tonndorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volksdorf" title="Volksdorf">Volksdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wandsbek_(quarter)" title="Wandsbek (quarter)">Wandsbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wellingsb%C3%BCttel" title="Wellingsbüttel">Wellingsbüttel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wohldorf-Ohlstedt" title="Wohldorf-Ohlstedt">Wohldorf-Ohlstedt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-actareal_53-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actareal-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:AlsterPanorama.jpg" class="image" title="A panoramic view of the Hamburg skyline of the Binnenalster taken from Lombardsbrücke."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/AlsterPanorama.jpg/900px-AlsterPanorama.jpg" width="900" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/AlsterPanorama.jpg/1350px-AlsterPanorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/AlsterPanorama.jpg/1800px-AlsterPanorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7000" data-file-height="1472" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AlsterPanorama.jpg" title="File:AlsterPanorama.jpg"></a></div>
A panoramic view of the Hamburg skyline of the <a href="/wiki/Binnenalster" title="Binnenalster">Binnenalster</a> taken from <a href="/wiki/Lombardsbr%C3%BCcke" class="mw-redirect" title="Lombardsbrücke">Lombardsbrücke</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmaille_126_126b.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Palmaille_126_126b.JPG/220px-Palmaille_126_126b.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Palmaille_126_126b.JPG/330px-Palmaille_126_126b.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Palmaille_126_126b.JPG/440px-Palmaille_126_126b.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2880" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palmaille_126_126b.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Historicist Palmaille, <a href="/wiki/Altona,_Hamburg" title="Altona, Hamburg">Altona</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamburg has architecturally significant buildings in a wide range of styles and only a few <a href="/wiki/Skyscraper" title="Skyscraper">skyscrapers</a>. Churches are important landmarks, such as <a href="/wiki/St._Nikolai,_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Nikolai, Hamburg">St Nicholas'</a>, which for a short time in the 19th century was the world's tallest building. The skyline features the tall spires of the most important churches (<i>Hauptkirchen</i>) <a href="/wiki/St._Michaelis_Church,_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Michaelis Church, Hamburg">St Michael's</a> (nicknamed "Michel"), <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church,_Hamburg" title="St. Peter's Church, Hamburg">St Peter's</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Jacobi,_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Jacobi, Hamburg">St James's</a> (<i>St. Jacobi</i>) and <a href="/wiki/St._Catherine%27s_Church,_Hamburg" title="St. Catherine's Church, Hamburg">St. Catherine's</a> covered with copper plates, and the <a href="/wiki/Heinrich-Hertz-Turm" class="mw-redirect" title="Heinrich-Hertz-Turm">Heinrich-Hertz-Turm</a>, the radio and television tower (no longer publicly accessible).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg/220px-Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg/330px-Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg/440px-Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="3330" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chilehaus_-_Hamburg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Chilehaus" title="Chilehaus">Chilehaus</a> with a typical <a href="/wiki/Brick_Expressionism" title="Brick Expressionism">brick expressionist</a> façade.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The many <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Hamburg" title="List of rivers of Hamburg">streams, rivers and canals</a> are crossed by <a href="/wiki/List_of_bridges_in_Hamburg" title="List of bridges in Hamburg">some 2,500 bridges</a>, more than <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a> put together.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Hamburg has more bridges inside its city limits than any other city in the world and more canals than Amsterdam and Venice combined.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6hlbrandbr%C3%BCcke" class="mw-redirect" title="Köhlbrandbrücke">Köhlbrandbrücke</a>, Freihafen Elbbrücken, and Lombardsbrücke and Kennedybrücke dividing Binnenalster from Aussenalster are important roadways.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Rathaus" title="Hamburg Rathaus">town hall</a> is a richly decorated Neo-Renaissance building finished in 1897. The tower is 112 metres (367&#160;ft) high. Its façade, 111&#160;m (364&#160;ft) long, depicts the emperors of the Holy Roman Empire, since Hamburg was, as a Free Imperial City, only under the sovereignty of the emperor.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Chilehaus" title="Chilehaus">Chilehaus</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Brick_Expressionism" title="Brick Expressionism">brick expressionist</a> office building built in 1922 and designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Johann_Friedrich_H%C3%B6ger" title="Johann Friedrich Höger">Fritz Höger</a>, is shaped like an ocean liner.</p>
<p>Europe's largest urban development since 2008, the <a href="/wiki/HafenCity" title="HafenCity">HafenCity</a>, will house about 10,000 inhabitants and 15,000 workers. The plan includes designs by <a href="/wiki/Rem_Koolhaas" title="Rem Koolhaas">Rem Koolhaas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renzo_Piano" title="Renzo Piano">Renzo Piano</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Elbphilharmonie" title="Elbphilharmonie">Elbphilharmonie</a> <i>(Elbe Philharmonic Hall)</i>, opened in January 2017, houses concerts in a sail-shaped building on top of an old warehouse, designed by architects <i><a href="/wiki/Herzog_%26_de_Meuron" title="Herzog &amp; de Meuron">Herzog &amp; de Meuron</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The many parks are distributed over the whole city, which makes Hamburg a very verdant city. The biggest parks are the <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Stadtpark" title="Hamburg Stadtpark">Stadtpark</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Ohlsdorf_Cemetery" title="Ohlsdorf Cemetery">Ohlsdorf Cemetery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Planten_un_Blomen" title="Planten un Blomen">Planten un Blomen</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Stadtpark" title="Hamburg Stadtpark">Stadtpark</a></i>, Hamburg's "Central Park", has a great lawn and a huge water tower, which houses one of Europe's biggest <a href="/wiki/Planetarium" title="Planetarium">planetaria</a>. The park and its buildings were designed by <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Schumacher_(architect)" title="Fritz Schumacher (architect)">Fritz Schumacher</a> in the 1910s.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_and_gardens_in_Hamburg" title="List of parks and gardens in Hamburg">List of parks and gardens in Hamburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg/220px-Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg/330px-Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg/440px-Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3330" data-file-height="2089" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wasserlichtkonzert_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Water-light concert at <i><a href="/wiki/Planten_un_Blomen" title="Planten un Blomen">Planten un Blomen</a></i> park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The lavish and spacious <i><a href="/wiki/Planten_un_Blomen" title="Planten un Blomen">Planten un Blomen</a></i> park (Low German dialect for "plants and flowers") located in the centre of Hamburg is the green heart of the city. Within the park you can find various thematic gardens, the biggest Japanese garden in Germany and The <i><a href="/wiki/Alter_Botanischer_Garten_Hamburg" title="Alter Botanischer Garten Hamburg">Alter Botanischer Garten Hamburg</a></i> which is a historic <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a>, that now consists primarily of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse" title="Greenhouse">greenhouses</a>.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten Hamburg">Botanischer Garten Hamburg</a></i> is a modern <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a> maintained by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hamburg" title="University of Hamburg">University of Hamburg</a>. Besides these, there are many more big and small parks. In 2010 Hamburg was voted "greenest city of Europe" by the <a href="/wiki/EU_commission" class="mw-redirect" title="EU commission">EU commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> In 2014 Hamburg celebrated a birthday of park culture, where many parks were reconstructed and cleaned up. Moreover, every year there are the famous water-light-concerts in the <i><a href="/wiki/Planten_un_Blomen" title="Planten un Blomen">Planten un Blomen</a></i> park from May to early October.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_contemporary_life">Culture and contemporary life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture and contemporary life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hamburg has more than 40 theatres, 60 museums and 100 music venues and clubs. In 2005, more than 18 million people visited concerts, exhibitions, theatres, cinemas, museums, and cultural events. More than 8,552 taxable companies (average size 3.16 employees) were engaged in the culture sector, which includes music, performing arts and literature. There are five companies in the creative sector per thousand residents (as compared to three in Berlin and 37 in London).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> Hamburg has entered the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital_Award" title="European Green Capital Award">European Green Capital Award</a> scheme, and was awarded the title of European Green Capital for 2011.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatres">Theatres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Theatres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_theatres_in_Hamburg" title="List of theatres in Hamburg">List of theatres in Hamburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg/220px-Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg/330px-Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg/440px-Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="610" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_Deutsches_Schauspielhaus_01_KMJ.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Schauspielhaus" title="Deutsches Schauspielhaus">Deutsches Schauspielhaus</a> in the St. Georg quarter</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg/220px-Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg/330px-Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg/440px-Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3453" data-file-height="5179" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Die_Elbphilharmonie_-_21.07.2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 110-metre-high (361-foot) <a href="/wiki/Elbphilharmonie" title="Elbphilharmonie">Elbphilharmonie</a> concert hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state-owned <i><a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Schauspielhaus" title="Deutsches Schauspielhaus">Deutsches Schauspielhaus</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Thalia_Theatre_(Hamburg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Thalia Theatre (Hamburg)">Thalia Theatre</a>, "Ohnsorg Theatre", "Schmidts Tivoli" and the <i>Kampnagel</i> are well-known theatres.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_English_Theatre_of_Hamburg" title="The English Theatre of Hamburg">The English Theatre of Hamburg</a><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> near U3 Mundsburg station was established in 1976 and is the oldest professional English-speaking theatre in Germany, and has exclusively English native-speaking actors in its company.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Hamburg" title="List of museums in Hamburg">List of museums in Hamburg</a></div>
<p>Hamburg has several large museums and galleries showing classical and contemporary art, for example the <a href="/wiki/Kunsthalle_Hamburg" title="Kunsthalle Hamburg">Kunsthalle Hamburg</a> with its contemporary art gallery (<i>Galerie der Gegenwart</i>), the Museum for Art and Industry (<i><a href="/wiki/Museum_f%C3%BCr_Kunst_und_Gewerbe_Hamburg" title="Museum für Kunst und Gewerbe Hamburg">Museum für Kunst und Gewerbe</a></i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Deichtorhallen" title="Deichtorhallen">Deichtorhallen</a>/House of Photography. The <a href="/wiki/Internationales_Maritimes_Museum_Hamburg" title="Internationales Maritimes Museum Hamburg">Internationales Maritimes Museum Hamburg</a> opened in the HafenCity quarter in 2008. There are various specialised museums in Hamburg, such as the Archaeological Museum Hamburg (<i><a href="/wiki/Arch%C3%A4ologisches_Museum_Hamburg" title="Archäologisches Museum Hamburg">Archäologisches Museum Hamburg</a></i>) in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Harburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Harburg">Hamburg-Harburg</a>, the Museum of Labour (<i>Museum der Arbeit</i>), and several museums of local history, for example the Kiekeberg Open Air Museum (<i>Freilichtmuseum am <a href="/wiki/Kiekeberg" title="Kiekeberg">Kiekeberg</a></i>). Two <i>museum ships</i> near Landungsbrücken bear witness to the freight ship (<i><a href="/wiki/Cap_San_Diego" title="Cap San Diego">Cap San Diego</a></i>) and cargo sailing ship era (<i><a href="/wiki/Rickmer_Rickmers" title="Rickmer Rickmers">Rickmer Rickmers</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> The world's largest model railway museum <a href="/wiki/Miniatur_Wunderland" title="Miniatur Wunderland">Miniatur Wunderland</a> with 15.4&#160;km (9.57&#160;mi) total railway length is also situated near Landungsbrücken in a former warehouse.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/BallinStadt" title="BallinStadt">BallinStadt</a> Emigration City</i> is dedicated to the millions of Europeans who emigrated to North and South America between 1850 and 1939. Visitors descending from those overseas emigrants may search for their ancestors at computer terminals.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hamburg_State_Opera" title="Hamburg State Opera">Hamburg State Opera</a> is a leading opera company. Its orchestra is the <a href="/wiki/Philharmoniker_Hamburg" title="Philharmoniker Hamburg">Philharmoniker Hamburg</a>. The city's other well-known orchestra is the <a href="/wiki/NDR_Elbphilharmonie_Orchestra" title="NDR Elbphilharmonie Orchestra">NDR Elbphilharmonie Orchestra</a>. The main concert venue is the <a href="/wiki/Laeiszhalle" title="Laeiszhalle">Laeiszhalle</a>, <i>Musikhalle Hamburg</i>, pending completion of the new <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Philharmonic_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Elbe Philharmonic Hall">Elbe Philharmonic Hall</a>. The Laeiszhalle also houses a third orchestra, the <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Symphoniker" title="Hamburger Symphoniker">Hamburger Symphoniker</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gy%C3%B6rgy_Ligeti" title="György Ligeti">György Ligeti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Schnittke" title="Alfred Schnittke">Alfred Schnittke</a> taught at the <a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Musik_und_Theater_Hamburg" title="Hochschule für Musik und Theater Hamburg">Hochschule für Musik und Theater Hamburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the German premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Cats_(musical)" title="Cats (musical)">Cats</a></i> in 1986, there have always been <a href="/wiki/Musical_theatre" title="Musical theatre">musicals</a> running, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Phantom_of_the_Opera_(1986_musical)" title="The Phantom of the Opera (1986 musical)">The Phantom of the Opera</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(musical)" title="The Lion King (musical)">The Lion King</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Dancing#Stage_version" title="Dirty Dancing">Dirty Dancing</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dance_of_the_Vampires" title="Dance of the Vampires">Dance of the Vampires</a></i>. This density, the highest in Germany, is partly due to the major musical production company <i><a href="/wiki/Stage_Entertainment" title="Stage Entertainment">Stage Entertainment</a></i> being based in the city.</p>
<p>Hamburg is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a>, who spent his formative early years in the city, and the birthplace and home of the famous waltz composer <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Fetr%C3%A1s" title="Oscar Fetrás">Oscar Fetrás</a>, who wrote the well-known "Mondnacht auf der Alster" waltz.</p>
<p>Prior to the group's initial recording and widespread fame, Hamburg provided residency and performing venues for the <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_Hamburg" title="The Beatles in Hamburg">Beatles</a> from 1960 to 1962. Hamburg has nurtured a number of pop musicians. Identical twins <a href="/wiki/Bill_Kaulitz" title="Bill Kaulitz">Bill Kaulitz</a> and Tom Kaulitz from the rock band <a href="/wiki/Tokio_Hotel" title="Tokio Hotel">Tokio Hotel</a> live and maintain a recording studio in Hamburg, where they recorded their second and third albums, <a href="/wiki/Zimmer_483" title="Zimmer 483">Zimmer 483</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanoid" title="Humanoid">Humanoid</a>. Singer <a href="/wiki/Nena" title="Nena">Nena</a> also lives in Hamburg. There are German hip hop acts, such as <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCnf_Sterne_deluxe" title="Fünf Sterne deluxe">Fünf Sterne deluxe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samy_Deluxe" title="Samy Deluxe">Samy Deluxe</a>, Beginner and <a href="/wiki/Fettes_Brot" title="Fettes Brot">Fettes Brot</a>. There is a substantial <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a> scene, which gathers around the <a href="/wiki/Rote_Flora" title="Rote Flora">Rote Flora</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Squatting" title="Squatting">squatted</a> former theatre located in the Sternschanze. Hamburg is famous for an original kind of German <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative music</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Schule" title="Hamburger Schule">Hamburger Schule</a></i> ("Hamburg School"), a term used for bands like <a href="/wiki/Tocotronic" title="Tocotronic">Tocotronic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blumfeld" title="Blumfeld">Blumfeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomte_(band)" title="Tomte (band)">Tomte</a> or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kante_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kante (band) (page does not exist)">Kante</a>.</p>
<p>The city was a major centre for <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal music</a> in the 1980s. <a href="/wiki/Helloween" title="Helloween">Helloween</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Ray_(band)" title="Gamma Ray (band)">Gamma Ray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Running_Wild_(band)" title="Running Wild (band)">Running Wild</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grave_Digger_(band)" title="Grave Digger (band)">Grave Digger</a> started in Hamburg.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_rock" title="Industrial rock">industrial rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/KMFDM" title="KMFDM">KMFDM</a> was also formed in Hamburg, initially as a performance art project. The influences of these and other bands from the area helped establish the subgenre of <a href="/wiki/Power_metal" title="Power metal">power metal</a>.</p>
<p>Hamburg has a vibrant psychedelic trance community, with record labels such as <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Zone_Records" title="Spirit Zone Records">Spirit Zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_regular_events">Festivals and regular events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Festivals and regular events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg/220px-Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg/330px-Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg/440px-Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4491" data-file-height="2061" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburger_Hafengeburtstag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Annual <a href="/wiki/Hafengeburtstag" title="Hafengeburtstag">Hafengeburtstag</a> (Port Anniversary)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamburg is noted for several festivals and regular events. Some of them are street festivals, such as the <a href="/wiki/Gay_pride" title="Gay pride">gay pride</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Pride" title="Hamburg Pride">Hamburg Pride</a></i> festival<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> or the Alster fair,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> held at the <i><a href="/wiki/Binnenalster" title="Binnenalster">Binnenalster</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_DOM" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburger DOM">Hamburger DOM</a></i> is northern Germany's biggest fun fair, held three times a year.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hafengeburtstag" title="Hafengeburtstag">Hafengeburtstag</a></i> is a <a href="/wiki/Funfair" class="mw-redirect" title="Funfair">funfair</a> to honour the birthday of the port of Hamburg with a party and a ship parade.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> The biker's service in <a href="/wiki/St._Michaelis_Church,_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Michaelis Church, Hamburg">Saint Michael's Church</a> attracts tens of thousands of <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle" title="Motorcycle">bikers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> Christmas markets in December are held at the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Rathaus" title="Hamburg Rathaus">Hamburg Rathaus</a> square, among other places.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> The <i>long night of museums</i> offers one entrance fee for about 40 museums until midnight.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> The sixth <i>Festival of Cultures</i> was held in September 2008, celebrating multi-cultural life.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Filmfest_Hamburg" title="Filmfest Hamburg">Filmfest Hamburg</a> — a film festival originating from the 1950s <i>Film Days</i> (German: <i>Film Tage</i>) — presents a wide range of films.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The <i>Hamburg Messe and Congress</i> offers a venue for trade shows, such <i>hanseboot</i>, an international boat show, or <i>Du und deine Welt</i>, a large consumer products show.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> Regular sports events—some open to pro and amateur participants—are the cycling competition <a href="/wiki/EuroEyes_Cyclassics" title="EuroEyes Cyclassics">EuroEyes Cyclassics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Marathon" title="Hamburg Marathon">Hamburg Marathon</a>, the biggest marathon in Germany after Berlin,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> the tennis tournament <a href="/wiki/International_German_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="International German Open">Hamburg Masters</a> and equestrian events like the <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Derby" title="Deutsches Derby">Deutsches Derby</a>. Since 2007, Hamburg has the <a href="/wiki/Dockville" title="Dockville">Dockville</a> music and art festival. It takes place every year in summer in <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmsburg,_Hamburg" title="Wilhelmsburg, Hamburg">Wilhelmsburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg/220px-Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg/330px-Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg/440px-Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1943" data-file-height="1492" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scholle_mit_Speck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fried <a href="/wiki/Plaice" title="Plaice">plaice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finkenwerder" title="Finkenwerder">Finkenwerder</a> style</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Hamburg" title="Cuisine of Hamburg">Cuisine of Hamburg</a></div>
<p>Original Hamburg dishes are <i><a href="/wiki/Birnen,_Bohnen_und_Speck" title="Birnen, Bohnen und Speck">Birnen, Bohnen und Speck</a></i> (green beans cooked with pears and bacon),<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> <i>Aalsuppe</i> (<a href="/wiki/Hamburgisch_dialect" title="Hamburgisch dialect">Hamburgisch</a> <i>Oolsupp</i>) is often mistaken to be German for "eel soup" (<i>Aal</i>/<i>Ool</i> translated ‘eel’), but the name probably comes from the Low Saxon <i>allns</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[aˑlns]</span>, meaning "all", "everything and the kitchen sink", not necessarily eel. Today eel is often included to meet the expectations of unsuspecting diners.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> There is <i>Bratkartoffeln</i> (pan-fried potato slices), <i>Finkenwerder Scholle</i> (Low Saxon <i>Finkwarder Scholl</i>, pan-fried plaice), <i>Pannfisch</i> (pan-fried fish with mustard sauce),<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/R%C3%B8dgr%C3%B8d" title="Rødgrød">Rote Grütze</a></i> (Low Saxon <i>Rode Grütt</i>, related to Danish <i>rødgrød</i>, a type of summer pudding made mostly from berries and usually served with cream, like Danish <i>rødgrød med fløde</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Labskaus" title="Labskaus">Labskaus</a></i> (a mixture of corned beef, mashed potatoes and beetroot, a cousin of the Norwegian <i>lapskaus</i> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Scouse_(food)" title="Scouse (food)">lobscouse</a>, all offshoots off an old-time one-pot meal that used to be the main component of the common sailor's humdrum diet on the high seas).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Alsterwasser</i> (in reference to the city's river, the Alster) is the local name for a type of <a href="/wiki/Shandy" title="Shandy">shandy</a>, a concoction of equal parts of beer and carbonated lemonade (<i>Zitronenlimonade</i>), the lemonade being added to the beer.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is the curious regional dessert pastry called <a href="/wiki/Franzbr%C3%B6tchen" title="Franzbrötchen">Franzbrötchen</a>. Looking rather like a flattened croissant, it is similar in preparation but includes a cinnamon and sugar filling, often with raisins or brown sugar <a href="/wiki/Streusel" title="Streusel">streusel</a>. The name may also reflect to the roll's <a href="/wiki/Croissant" title="Croissant">croissant</a>-like appearance – <i>franz</i> appears to be a shortening of <i>französisch</i>, meaning "French", which would make a <i>Franzbrötchen</i> a "French roll." Ordinary bread rolls tend to be oval-shaped and of the French bread variety. The local name is <i>Schrippe</i> (scored lengthways) for the oval kind and, for the round kind, <i>Rundstück</i> ("round piece" rather than mainstream German <i>Brötchen</i>, diminutive form of <i>Brot</i> "bread"),<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> a relative of Denmark's <i>rundstykke</i>. In fact, while by no means identical, the cuisines of Hamburg and <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, especially of <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, have a lot in common. This also includes a predilection for open-faced sandwiches of all sorts, especially topped with cold-smoked or pickled fish.</p>
<p>The American <a href="/wiki/Hamburger" title="Hamburger">hamburger</a> may have developed from Hamburg's <i><a href="/wiki/Frikadeller" title="Frikadeller">Frikadeller</a></i>: a pan-fried patty (usually larger and thicker than its American counterpart) made from a mixture of ground beef, soaked <a href="/wiki/Staling" title="Staling">stale bread</a>, egg, chopped onion, salt and pepper, usually served with potatoes and vegetables like any other piece of meat, not usually on a bun. The Oxford Dictionary defined a <i>Hamburger steak</i> in 1802: a sometimes-smoked and -salted piece of meat, that, according to some sources, came from Hamburg to America.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> The name and food, "hamburger", has entered all English-speaking countries, and derivative words in non-English speaking countries.</p>
<p>There are restaurants which offer most of these dishes, especially in the <a href="/wiki/HafenCity" title="HafenCity">HafenCity</a>, which started being built in 2008 with 155 hectares (380 acres) and 13 quarters. This district increases the city centre by about 40%, with restaurants and apartments.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
