<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_culture">Alternative culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Alternative culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG/220px-Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG/330px-Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG/440px-Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rote_Flora_-_2014_-_seitlich.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rote Flora in the <a href="/wiki/Sternschanze" title="Sternschanze">Sternschanze</a> neighbourhood, Hamburg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamburg has long been a centre of alternative music and counter culture movements. The boroughs of <a href="/wiki/St._Pauli" title="St. Pauli">St. Pauli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sternschanze" title="Sternschanze">Sternschanze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Altona,_Hamburg" title="Altona, Hamburg">Altona</a> are known for being home to many radical left-wing and anarchist groups, culminating every year during the traditional May Day demonstrations.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rote_Flora" title="Rote Flora">Rote Flora</a> is a former theatre, which was squatted in 1989 in the wake of re-development plans for that area. Since then, the Rote Flora has become one of the most well-known strongholds against gentrification and a place for radical culture throughout Germany and Europe. Especially during the <a href="/wiki/33rd_G8_summit" title="33rd G8 summit">33rd G8 summit</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Heiligendamm" title="Heiligendamm">Heiligendamm</a>, the Rote Flora served as an important venue for organising the counter-protests that were taking place back then.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2017 G20 summit, which took place in Hamburg from 7–8 July that year, protestors clashed violently with the police in the Sternschanze area and particularly around the Rote Flora. On 7 July, several cars were set on fire and street barricades were erected to prevent the police from entering the area. In response to that, the police made heavy use of water cannons and tear gas in order to scatter the protestors. However, this was met with strong resistance by protestors, resulting in a total of 160 injured police and 75 arrested participants in the protests.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the summit, however, the Rote Flora issued a statement, in which it condemns the arbitrary acts of violence that were committed by some of the protestors whilst generally defending the right to use violence as a means of self-defence against police oppression. In particular, the spokesperson of the Rote Flora said that the autonomous cultural centre had a traditionally good relationship with its neighbours and local residents, since they were united in their fight against gentrification in that neighbourhood.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_culture">English culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: English culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg/220px-Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg/330px-Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg/440px-Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5080" data-file-height="3932" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammonia-Bad_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
English Theatre of Hamburg at Lerchenfeld 14</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are several English-speaking communities, such as Caledonian Society of Hamburg, The British Club Hamburg, British and Commonwealth Luncheon Club, Anglo-German Club <a href="/wiki/Eingetragener_Verein" class="mw-redirect" title="Eingetragener Verein">e.V.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> Professional Women's Forum,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> The British Decorative and Fine Arts Society, The English Speaking Union of the Commonwealth, The Scottish Country Dancers of Hamburg. There is also a thriving 400-year-old Anglican church community worshiping at <i>St Thomas Becket Church</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Further The Hamburg Players e. V. English Language Theatre Group, The <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Exiles_RFC" title="Hamburg Exiles RFC">Hamburg Exiles Rugby Club</a>, Several cricket clubs, The Morris Minor Register of Hamburg. Furthermore, the Anglo-Hanseatic Lodge No. 850 <sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> within the Grand Lodge of British Freemasons of Germany<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> under the United Grand Lodges of Germany <sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> works in Hamburg, and has a diverse expat membership.</p>
<p>American and international English-speaking organisations are The American Club of Hamburg <a href="/wiki/Eingetragener_Verein" class="mw-redirect" title="Eingetragener Verein">e.V.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> the American Women's Club of Hamburg,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> the English Speaking Union, and the German-American Women's Club.,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> The International Women's Club of Hamburg e. V.. Business themes are dealt with by <i>The American Chamber of Commerce</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Hamburg" title="International School of Hamburg">International School of Hamburg</a> serves school children.</p>
<p>A Hamburg saying, referring to its anglophile nature, is: "Wenn es in London anfängt zu regnen, spannen die Hamburger den Schirm auf." ... "When it starts raining in London, people in Hamburg open their umbrellas.".</p>
<p>A tribute to the British is that for German's extremely popular 18 minutes short intimate play "<a href="/wiki/Dinner_for_One" title="Dinner for One">Dinner For One - The 90th Birthday</a>". It was casted 1963 as a live act for TV in english language at NDR-Hamburg studios with Freddie Frinton and May Warden. The funny story is about a wealthy british lady, her buttler and four pretended guests celebrating her 90th birthday.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorials">Memorials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Memorials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A memorial for successful English engineer <a href="/wiki/William_Lindley" title="William Lindley">William Lindley</a>, who reorganized, beginning in 1842, the drinking water and sewage system and thus helped to fight against cholera, is near Baumwall train station in Vorsetzen street.</p>
<p>In 2009, more than 2,500 "stumbling blocks" <i>(<a href="/wiki/Stolpersteine" class="mw-redirect" title="Stolpersteine">Stolpersteine</a>)</i> were laid, engraved with the names of deported and murdered citizens. Inserted into the pavement in front of their former houses, the blocks draw attention to the victims of Nazi persecution.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003,_Hamburg,_B%C3%B6rse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003%2C_Hamburg%2C_B%C3%B6rse.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003%2C_Hamburg%2C_B%C3%B6rse.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003%2C_Hamburg%2C_B%C3%B6rse.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003%2C_Hamburg%2C_B%C3%B6rse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003%2C_Hamburg%2C_B%C3%B6rse.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003%2C_Hamburg%2C_B%C3%B6rse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="527" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F078953-0003,_Hamburg,_B%C3%B6rse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Stock_Exchange" title="Hamburg Stock Exchange">Hamburg Stock Exchange</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2007 <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) totaled €85.9 billion. The city has a relatively high employment rate, at 88 percent of the working-age population, employed in over 120,000 businesses.The average income of employees was €30,937.<sup id="cite_ref-Basisdaten_2007_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Basisdaten_2007-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking">Banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Banking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hamburg has for centuries been a commercial centre of Northern Europe, and is the most important <a href="/wiki/Banking" class="mw-redirect" title="Banking">banking</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Germany" title="Northern Germany">Northern Germany</a>. The city is the seat of <a href="/wiki/History_of_banking" title="History of banking">Germany's oldest bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Berenberg_Bank" title="Berenberg Bank">Berenberg Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/M.M.Warburg_%26_CO" class="mw-redirect" title="M.M.Warburg &amp; CO">M.M.Warburg &amp; CO</a> and <a href="/wiki/HSH_Nordbank" title="HSH Nordbank">HSH Nordbank</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Stock_Exchange" title="Hamburg Stock Exchange">Hamburg Stock Exchange</a> is the oldest of its kind in Germany.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_%283%29.jpg/170px-Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_%283%29.jpg" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_%283%29.jpg/255px-Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_%283%29.jpg/340px-Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankunft_der_Queen_Mary_2_in_Hamburg_-_panoramio_-_Arnold_Schott_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/RMS_Queen_Mary_2" title="RMS Queen Mary 2">Queen Mary 2</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Hamburg" title="Port of Hamburg">Port of Hamburg</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The most significant economic unit is the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Hamburg" title="Port of Hamburg">Port of Hamburg</a>, which ranks second to <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> in Europe and ninth worldwide with transshipments of 9.8 million&#160;<a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">twenty-foot equivalent units</a>&#160;(TEU) of cargo and 134 million tons of goods in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> After German reunification, Hamburg recovered the eastern portion of its hinterland, becoming by far the fastest-growing port in Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> International trade is also the reason for the large number of consulates in the city. Although situated 68 miles (110&#160;km) up the Elbe, it is considered a sea port due to its ability to handle large ocean-going vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_production">Industrial production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Industrial production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Heavy industry of Hamburg includes the making of steel, aluminium, copper and various large shipyards such as <a href="/wiki/Blohm_%2B_Voss" class="mw-redirect" title="Blohm + Voss">Blohm + Voss</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamburg, along with <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, is an important location of the civil <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> industry. <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>, which has an assembly plant in Finkenwerder, employs over 13,000&#160;people.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HafenCity">HafenCity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: HafenCity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg/220px-Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg/330px-Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg/440px-Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_-_Highflyer_-IMG-1414.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Western HafenCity area and <a href="/wiki/Speicherstadt" title="Speicherstadt">Speicherstadt</a> (UNESCO World Heritage)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/HafenCity" title="HafenCity">HafenCity</a> is Europe's largest urban development project and is located in the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Mitte" title="Hamburg-Mitte">Hamburg-Mitte</a> district. It consists of the area of the Great Grasbrook, the northern part of the former Elbe island <a href="/wiki/Grasbrook" class="mw-redirect" title="Grasbrook">Grasbrook</a>, and the warehouse district on the former Elbe island Kehrwieder and Wandrahm. It is bordered to the north, separated by the customs channel to Hamburg's city center, west and south by the Elbe and to the east, bounded by the upper harbor, <a href="/wiki/Rothenburgsort" title="Rothenburgsort">Rothenburgsort</a>. The district is full of rivers and streams and is surrounded by channels, and has a total area of about 2.2&#160;square-kilometers.</p>
<p>HafenCity has 155 hectares in the area formerly belonging to the free port north of the Great Grasbrook. Residential units for up to 12,000 people are planned to be built on the site by around the mid-2020s, and jobs for up to 40,000 people, mainly in the office sector, should be created. It is the largest ongoing urban development project in Hamburg.</p>
<p>Construction work started in 2003, and in 2009 the first part of the urban development project was finished with the completion of the Dalmannkai / Sandtorkai neighborhood – which is the first stage of the HafenCity project. According to the person responsible for the development and commercialization of HafenCity, <i>HafenCity Hamburg GmbH</i>, half of the master plan underlying structural construction is already completed, whereas the other half is either under construction or is in the construction preparation stages.</p>
<p>Many companies operating in <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">E-Commerce</a> have moved into HafenCity or started there. In addition to cruise agents such as the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.1000kreuzfahrten.de/">CaptainTravel GmbH</a> many <a href="/wiki/Start-up_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Start-up company">start-up companies</a> that have no direct connection to the port or ships can be found in HafenCity.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/Hamburg_logo.jpg/220px-Hamburg_logo.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c8/Hamburg_logo.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="191" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hamburg city logo</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg/220px-HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg/330px-HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg/440px-HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2094" data-file-height="1396" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HH_Neuer_Wall_Dezember_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Neuer_Wall" title="Neuer Wall">Neuer Wall</a>, one of Europe's most luxurious shopping streets</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2007, more than 3,985,105&#160;visitors with 7,402,423&#160;overnight stays visited the city.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> The tourism sector employs more than 175,000 people full-time and brings in <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a> of almost €9 billion, making the tourism industry a major economic force in the Hamburg Metropolitan Region. Hamburg has one of the fastest-growing tourism industries in Germany. From 2001 to 2007, the overnight stays in the city increased by 55.2% (Berlin +52.7%, <a href="/wiki/Mecklenburg-Vorpommern" title="Mecklenburg-Vorpommern">Mecklenburg-Vorpommern</a> +33%).<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>A typical Hamburg visit includes a tour of the city hall and the grand church <a href="/wiki/St._Michaelis_Church,_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Michaelis Church, Hamburg">St. Michaelis</a> (called the <i>Michel</i>), and visiting the old warehouse district (<i><a href="/wiki/Speicherstadt" title="Speicherstadt">Speicherstadt</a></i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Landungsbr%C3%BCcken" class="mw-redirect" title="Landungsbrücken">harbour promenade</a> (<i>Landungsbrücken</i>). Sightseeing buses connect these points of interest. As Hamburg is one of the world's largest harbours many visitors take one of the harbour and/or canal boat tours (<i>Große Hafenrundfahrt</i>, <i>Fleetfahrt</i>) which start from the <i>Landungsbrücken</i>. Major destinations also include <a href="/wiki/Museum" title="Museum">museums</a>.</p>
<p>The area of <a href="/wiki/Reeperbahn" title="Reeperbahn">Reeperbahn</a> in the quarter <a href="/wiki/St._Pauli" title="St. Pauli">St. Pauli</a> is Europe's largest red light district and home of strip clubs, brothels, bars and nightclubs. The singer and actor <a href="/wiki/Hans_Albers" title="Hans Albers">Hans Albers</a> is strongly associated with St. Pauli, and wrote the neighbourhood's unofficial anthem, "Auf der Reeperbahn Nachts um Halb Eins" ("<a href="/wiki/On_the_Reeperbahn_at_Half_Past_Midnight_(song)" title="On the Reeperbahn at Half Past Midnight (song)">On the Reeperbahn at Half Past Midnight</a>") in the 1940s. <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> had stints on the Reeperbahn early in their careers. Others prefer the laid-back neighbourhood <i>Schanze</i> with its street cafés, or a barbecue on one of the beaches along the river Elbe. Hamburg's famous zoo, the <a href="/wiki/Tierpark_Hagenbeck" title="Tierpark Hagenbeck">Tierpark Hagenbeck</a>, was founded in 1907 by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Hagenbeck" title="Carl Hagenbeck">Carl Hagenbeck</a> as the first zoo with moated, barless enclosures.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005, the average visitor spent two nights in Hamburg.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The majority of visitors come from Germany. Most foreigners are European, especially from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (171,000 overnight stays), <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (about 143,000 overnight stays), <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> (about 137,000 overnight stays) and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (about 80,000 overnight stays). The largest group from outside Europe comes from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (129,000 overnight stays).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/RMS_Queen_Mary_2" title="RMS Queen Mary 2">Queen Mary 2</a> has docked regularly since 2004, and there were six departures planned from 2010 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiegel_building_Hamburg,_Ericusspitze,_at_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Spiegel_building_Hamburg%2C_Ericusspitze%2C_at_night.jpg/220px-Spiegel_building_Hamburg%2C_Ericusspitze%2C_at_night.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Spiegel_building_Hamburg%2C_Ericusspitze%2C_at_night.jpg/330px-Spiegel_building_Hamburg%2C_Ericusspitze%2C_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Spiegel_building_Hamburg%2C_Ericusspitze%2C_at_night.jpg/440px-Spiegel_building_Hamburg%2C_Ericusspitze%2C_at_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spiegel_building_Hamburg,_Ericusspitze,_at_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a> headquarters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Media businesses employ over 70,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Norddeutscher_Rundfunk" title="Norddeutscher Rundfunk">Norddeutscher Rundfunk</a> which includes the television station <a href="/wiki/NDR_Fernsehen" title="NDR Fernsehen">NDR Fernsehen</a> is based in Hamburg, as are the commercial television station <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg_1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hamburg 1 (page does not exist)">Hamburg 1</a></i>, the Christian television station <i><a href="/wiki/Bibel_TV" title="Bibel TV">Bibel TV</a></i> and the civil media outlet <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tide_TV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tide TV (page does not exist)">Tide TV</a></i>. There are regional radio stations such as <a href="/wiki/Radio_Hamburg" title="Radio Hamburg">Radio Hamburg</a>. Some of Germany's largest publishing companies, <a href="/wiki/Axel_Springer_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Axel Springer AG">Axel Springer AG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gruner_%2B_Jahr" title="Gruner + Jahr">Gruner + Jahr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bauer_Media_Group" title="Bauer Media Group">Bauer Media Group</a> are located in the city. Many national newspapers and magazines such as <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Zeit" title="Die Zeit">Die Zeit</a></i> are produced in Hamburg, as well as some special-interest newspapers such as <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times_Deutschland" title="Financial Times Deutschland">Financial Times Deutschland</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Abendblatt" title="Hamburger Abendblatt">Hamburger Abendblatt</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Morgenpost" title="Hamburger Morgenpost">Hamburger Morgenpost</a></i> are daily regional newspapers with a large circulation. There are music publishers, such as <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a> Germany, and <a href="/wiki/Information_and_communication_technologies" class="mw-redirect" title="Information and communication technologies">ICT</a> firms such as <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> Germany. The Internet and telecommunications company <a href="/wiki/HanseNet" class="mw-redirect" title="HanseNet">HanseNet</a>, which sells DSL Internet access under the Alice brand, has its headquarters in Hamburg.</p>
<p>Hamburg was one of the locations for the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond (film series)">James Bond series</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Dies" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">Tomorrow Never Dies</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Reeperbahn" title="Reeperbahn">Reeperbahn</a></i> has been the location for many scenes, including the 1994 Beatles film <i><a href="/wiki/Backbeat_(film)" title="Backbeat (film)">Backbeat</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> The film <i><a href="/wiki/A_Most_Wanted_Man_(film)" title="A Most Wanted Man (film)">A Most Wanted Man</a></i> was set in and filmed in Hamburg. Hamburg was also shown in <i><a href="/wiki/An_American_Tail" title="An American Tail">An American Tail</a></i> where Fievel Mousekewitz and his family immigrate to America in the hopes to escape cats.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_systems">Health systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Health systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hamburg has 54 hospitals. The <a href="/wiki/University_Medical_Center_Hamburg-Eppendorf" title="University Medical Center Hamburg-Eppendorf">University Medical Center Hamburg-Eppendorf</a>, with about 1,450 beds, houses a large medical school. There are also smaller private hospitals. On 1 January 2011 there were about 11,350 hospital beds.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> The city had 5,663 physicians in private practice and 456 pharmacies in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Hamburg" title="Transport in Hamburg">Transport in Hamburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg/220px-CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg/330px-CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg/440px-CTB-CTW_Port_of_Hamburg-Waltershof.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="333" /></a>

</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg/220px-Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg/330px-Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg/440px-Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="817" data-file-height="545" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg.NorderElbbr%C3%BCcken.2.wmt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neue and Freihafen-Elbbrücke</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamburg is a major transportation hub, connected to four <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahnen</a> (motorways) and the most important railway junction on the route to Scandinavia.</p>
<p>Bridges and tunnels connect the northern and southern parts of the city, such as the <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Tunnel_(1911)" title="Elbe Tunnel (1911)">old Elbe Tunnel</a> (<i>Alter Elbtunnel</i>) or St. Pauli Elbtunnel (official name) which opened in 1911, now is major tourist sight, and the <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Tunnel_(1975)" title="Elbe Tunnel (1975)">Elbe Tunnel</a> (<i>Elbtunnel</i>) the crossing of a <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_7" title="Bundesautobahn 7">motorway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg Airport</a> is the oldest airport in Germany still in operation.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> There is also the smaller <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Finkenwerder_Airport" title="Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport">Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport</a>, used only as a company airport for <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>. Some airlines market <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck_Airport" title="Lübeck Airport">Lübeck Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BCbeck" title="Lübeck">Lübeck</a> as serving Hamburg.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamburg's <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_Germany" title="Vehicle registration plates of Germany">licence plate</a> prefix was "HH" (Hansestadt Hamburg; English: Hanseatic City of Hamburg) between 1906 and 1945 and from 1956, rather than the single letter normally used for large cities since the federal registration reform in 1956, such as B for Berlin or M for Munich. "H" was Hamburg's prefix in the years between 1945 and 1947 (used by <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a> since 1956);<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">Public transport</a> by rail, bus and ship is organised by the <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Verkehrsverbund" title="Hamburger Verkehrsverbund">Hamburger Verkehrsverbund</a></i> ("Hamburg transit authority") (HVV). Tickets sold by one company are valid on all other HVV companies' services. The HVV was the first organisation of this kind worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ten mass transit rail lines across the city are the backbone of public transport. The <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_S-Bahn" title="Hamburg S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a> (heavy railway system) comprises six lines and the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_U-Bahn" title="Hamburg U-Bahn">U-Bahn</a> four lines – <i>U-Bahn</i> is short for <i>Untergrundbahn</i> (underground railway). Approximately 41&#160;km (25&#160;mi) of 101&#160;km (63&#160;mi) of the U-Bahn is underground; most is on embankments or viaduct or at ground level. Older residents still speak of the system as <i>Hochbahn</i> (elevated railway), also because the operating company of the subway is the <i><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_Hochbahn" title="Hamburger Hochbahn">Hamburger Hochbahn</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/AKN_Eisenbahn" title="AKN Eisenbahn">AKN railway</a> connects satellite towns in Schleswig-Holstein to the city. On some routes regional trains of Germany's major railway company <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn AG</a> and the regional <i><a href="/wiki/Metronom_Eisenbahngesellschaft" title="Metronom Eisenbahngesellschaft">metronom</a></i> trains may be used with an HVV ticket. Except at the four bigger stations of the city, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Hauptbahnhof" title="Hamburg Hauptbahnhof">Hauptbahnhof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Dammtor_station" title="Hamburg Dammtor station">Dammtor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Altona_station" title="Hamburg-Altona station">Altona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Harburg_station" title="Hamburg-Harburg station">Harburg</a> regional trains do not stop inside the city. The <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Hamburg" title="Trams in Hamburg">tram system</a> was opened in 1866 and shut down in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-tramway-atlas-germany-1996_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tramway-atlas-germany-1996-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gaps in the rail network are filled by more than 600 bus routes, operated by single-deck two-, three- and four-axle diesel buses. Hamburg has no <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trams</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybuses</a>, but has hydrogen-fueled buses operating pilot services. The buses run frequently during working hours, with buses on some so-called MetroBus routes as often as every 2 minutes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On special weekday night lines the intervals can be 30 minutes or longer, on normal days (Monday-Friday) the normal buses stop running at night. (MetroBuses run all around the clock, every day at the year at least every half-hour.)</p>
<p>There are six ferry lines along the <a href="/wiki/River_Elbe" class="mw-redirect" title="River Elbe">River Elbe</a>, operated by <i><a href="/wiki/HADAG_Seetouristik_und_F%C3%A4hrdienst" class="mw-redirect" title="HADAG Seetouristik und Fährdienst">HADAG</a></i>, that fall under the aegis of the HVV. While mainly used by citizens and dock workers, they can also be used for sightseeing tours.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A321_final_assembly_(9351765668).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/A321_final_assembly_%289351765668%29.jpg/220px-A321_final_assembly_%289351765668%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/A321_final_assembly_%289351765668%29.jpg/330px-A321_final_assembly_%289351765668%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/A321_final_assembly_%289351765668%29.jpg/440px-A321_final_assembly_%289351765668%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A321_final_assembly_(9351765668).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a> on <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">final assembly line</a> 3 in the Airbus plant at <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Finkenwerder_Airport" title="Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport">Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The international airport at Hamburg Fuhlsbüttel, official name "<a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg Airport Helmut Schmidt</a>" (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">IATA</a>: HAM, <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">ICAO</a>: EDDH) is the fifth biggest and oldest airport in Germany, having been established in 1912 and located about 5 miles (8 kilometres) from the city centre. About 60 airlines provide service to 125 destination airports, including some long distance destinations like <a href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey" title="Newark, New Jersey">Newark, New Jersey</a> on <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> on <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> on <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air" title="Iran Air">Iran Air</a>; <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> is the hub carrier, with the most flights, followed by <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a>, and Lufthansa operates one of its biggest <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Technik" title="Lufthansa Technik">maintenance facilities</a> at the Hamburg airport. The second airport is located in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg-Finkenwerder" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg-Finkenwerder">Hamburg-Finkenwerder</a>, official name <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Finkenwerder_Airport" title="Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport">Hamburg Finkenwerder Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">IATA</a>: XFW, <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">ICAO</a>: EDHI). It is about 10&#160;km (6&#160;mi) from the city centre and is a nonpublic airport for the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_Operations_GmbH&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Airbus Operations GmbH (page does not exist)">Airbus</a> plant. It is the second biggest Airbus plant, after <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, and the third biggest aviation manufacturing plant after <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> and Toulouse; the plant houses the final assembly lines for A318, A319, A320, A321 and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">A380</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Transportation_Statistics">Public Transportation Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Public Transportation Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Hamburg, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 58 min. 16% of public transit riders, ride for more than two hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 11 min, while 11% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 8.9&#160;km, while 21% travel for over 12&#160;km in a single direction.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Electricity for Hamburg and Northern Germany is largely provided by <i><a href="/wiki/Vattenfall" title="Vattenfall">Vattenfall Europe</a></i>, formerly the state-owned <i>Hamburgische Electricitäts-Werke</i>. Vattenfall Europe used to operate the <a href="/wiki/Brunsb%C3%BCttel_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Brunsbüttel Nuclear Power Plant">Brunsbüttel Nuclear Power Plant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%BCmmel_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Krümmel Nuclear Power Plant">Krümmel Nuclear Power Plant</a>, both taken out of service as part of the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_Germany#Closures_and_phase-out" title="Nuclear power in Germany">nuclear power phase-out</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a> operates the <a href="/wiki/Brokdorf_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Brokdorf Nuclear Power Plant">Brokdorf Nuclear Power Plant</a> near Hamburg. There are also the coal-fired <a href="/wiki/Wedel_Power_Station" title="Wedel Power Station">Wedel</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tiefstack_Power_Station&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tiefstack Power Station (page does not exist)">Tiefstack</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moorburg_Power_Station&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Moorburg Power Station (page does not exist)">Moorburg Power Stations</a>, and the fuel-cell power plant in the HafenCity quarter. <i>VERA Klärschlammverbrennung</i> uses the biosolids of the Hamburg wastewater treatment plant; the <i>Pumpspeicherwerk Geesthacht</i> is a pump storage power plant and a solid waste combustion power station is <i>Müllverwertung Borsigstraße</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Hamburg" title="Sport in Hamburg">Sport in Hamburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg/220px-Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg/330px-Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg/440px-Hamburg_City_Man_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg/220px-RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg/330px-RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg/440px-RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RK_1009_9831_Volksparkstadion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Volksparkstadion" title="Volksparkstadion">Volksparkstadion</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hamburg is sometimes called Germany's capital of sport since no other city has more first-league teams and international sports events.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team in the <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a>. The HSV is the oldest team of the Bundesliga, playing in the league since its beginning in 1963. HSV is a six-time German champion, a three-time German cup winner and triumphed in the European Cup in 1983, and has played in the group stages of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> twice: in 2000/2001 and in 2006/2007. They play at the <a href="/wiki/Volksparkstadion" title="Volksparkstadion">Volksparkstadion</a> (average attendance in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Bundesliga" title="2012–13 Bundesliga">12/13 season</a> was 52,916). In addition, <a href="/wiki/FC_St._Pauli" title="FC St. Pauli">FC St. Pauli</a> was a <a href="/wiki/2._Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="2. Fußball-Bundesliga">second division</a> football club that came in second place in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="2009–10 Fußball-Bundesliga">2009/2010 season</a> and qualified to play alongside <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fußball-Bundesliga">first division</a> for the first time since the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Fu%C3%9Fball-Bundesliga" class="mw-redirect" title="2001–02 Fußball-Bundesliga">2001–02 season</a>. St. Pauli's home games take place at the <a href="/wiki/Millerntor-Stadion" title="Millerntor-Stadion">Millerntor-Stadion</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Freezers" title="Hamburg Freezers">Hamburg Freezers</a> represented Hamburg until 2016 in the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Eishockey_Liga" title="Deutsche Eishockey Liga">DEL</a>, the premier <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> league in Germany.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/HSV_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="HSV Hamburg">HSV Handball</a> represented Hamburg until 2016 in the German <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(handball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesliga (handball)">handball league</a>. In 2007, HSV Handball won the European Cupwinners Cup. The Club won the league in the 2010/11 season and had an average attandence of 10.690 in the <a href="/wiki/O2_World_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="O2 World Hamburg">O2 World Hamburg</a> the same year. The most recent success for the team was the <a href="/wiki/EHF_Champions_League" title="EHF Champions League">EHF Champions League</a> win in 2013. Since 2014 the club has suffered from economic problems and was almost not allowed the playing licence for the 2014–15 season. But due to economic support from the former club president/sponsor Andreas Rudolf the club was allowed the licence in the last minute. On 20 January 2016 however, their licence was removed due to violations following the continued economic struggles. In 2016–17 they are not allowed to play in the first or second league.</p>
<p>The <i>BCJ Hamburg</i> played in the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Bundesliga" title="Basketball Bundesliga">Basketball Bundesliga</a> from 1999 to 2001. Since then, teams from Hamburg have attempted to return to Germany's elite league. The recently founded <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Towers" title="Hamburg Towers">Hamburg Towers</a> have already established themselves as one of the main teams in Germany's second division <a href="/wiki/ProA" title="ProA">ProA</a> and aim to take on the heritage of the BCJ Hamburg. The Towers play their home games at the <i>Inselparkhalle</i> in <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmsburg,_Hamburg" title="Wilhelmsburg, Hamburg">Wilhelmsburg</a>.</p>
<p>Hamburg is the nation's <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> capital and dominates the men's as well as the women's Bundesliga. Hamburg hosts many top teams such as Uhlenhorster Hockey Club, Harvesterhuder Hockey Club and Club An Der Alster.</p>
<p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg_Warriors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hamburg Warriors (page does not exist)">Hamburg Warriors</a> are one of Germany's top lacrosse clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> The club has grown immensely in the last several years and includes at least one youth team, three men's, and two women's teams. The team participates in the Deutsch Lacrosse Verein. The Hamburg Warriors are part of the Harvestehuder Tennis- und Hockey-Club e.V (HTHC).<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are also the <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football_in_Germany#Hamburg_Dockers" title="Australian rules football in Germany">Hamburg Dockers</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> club.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> The FC St. Pauli team dominates women's rugby in Germany. Other first-league teams include VT Aurubis Hamburg (Volleyball), Hamburger Polo Club, and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Blue_Devils" title="Hamburg Blue Devils">Hamburg Blue Devils</a> (American Football).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> There are also several minority sports clubs, including four <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> clubs.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg/220px-Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg/330px-Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg/440px-Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Court_Am_Rothenbaum_Sliding_Roof.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Am_Rothenbaum" title="Am Rothenbaum">Am Rothenbaum</a> is the main tennis stadium of the <a href="/wiki/International_German_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="International German Open">International German Open</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Centre Court of the Tennis <a href="/wiki/Am_Rothenbaum" title="Am Rothenbaum">Am Rothenbaum</a> venue, with a capacity of 13,200 people, is the largest in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamburg also hosts <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a> events at <i>Reitstadion <a href="/wiki/Klein_Flottbek" title="Klein Flottbek">Klein Flottbek</a></i> (Deutsches Derby in jumping and dressage) and <i><a href="/wiki/Horner_Rennbahn" title="Horner Rennbahn">Horner Rennbahn</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Derby" title="Deutsches Derby">Deutsches Derby</a> <a href="/wiki/Flat_racing" title="Flat racing">flat racing</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Besides Hamburg owns the famous <a href="/wiki/Harness_racing" title="Harness racing">harness racing</a> track "<a href="/wiki/Trabrennbahn_Bahrenfeld" title="Trabrennbahn Bahrenfeld">Trabrennbahn Bahrenfeld</a>". The Hamburg Marathon is the biggest <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">marathon</a> in Germany after Berlin's. In 2008 23,230 participants were registered.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> World Cup events in cycling, the UCI ProTour competition <a href="/wiki/EuroEyes_Cyclassics" title="EuroEyes Cyclassics">EuroEyes Cyclassics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a> <a href="/wiki/International_Triathlon_Union" title="International Triathlon Union">ITU</a> World Cup event <i>Hamburg City Man</i> are also held in here.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Volksparkstadion was used as a site for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>. In 2010 UEFA held the final of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> in the arena.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hamburg was applying for <a href="/wiki/2024_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="2024 Olympic Games">2024 Olympic Games</a>. However 51.7 percent of those participating in the <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> (only Hamburg's residents) in November 2015 had decided against continuing Hamburg's bid to host the 2024 Olympics. Meanwhile, Hamburg's partner city <a href="/wiki/Kiel" title="Kiel">Kiel</a> voted in favour of hosting the event, with almost 66 percent of all participants supporting the bid. Opponents of the bid had argued that hosting the 33rd Olympic Games would cost the city too much in public funds.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Hamburg" title="Education in Hamburg">Education in Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Germany" title="Education in Germany">Education in Germany</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg/220px-2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg/330px-2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg/440px-2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1673" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2013-06-08_Projekt_Hei%C3%9Fluftballon_DSCF0784.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/University_of_Hamburg" title="University of Hamburg">University of Hamburg</a> main building</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hh-budgepalais.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Hh-budgepalais.jpg/220px-Hh-budgepalais.jpg" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Hh-budgepalais.jpg/330px-Hh-budgepalais.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Hh-budgepalais.jpg/440px-Hh-budgepalais.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2572" data-file-height="1368" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hh-budgepalais.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Musik_und_Theater_Hamburg" title="Hochschule für Musik und Theater Hamburg">University of Music and Theatre</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The school system is managed by the Ministry of Schools and Vocational Training (<i>Behörde für Schule und Berufsbildung</i>). The system had approximately 160,000 students in 245 <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">primary schools</a> and 195 <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary schools</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> There are 33 public libraries in Hamburg proper.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Seventeen universities are located in Hamburg, with about 70,000 university students in total, including 9,000 resident aliens. Six universities are public, including the largest, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hamburg" title="University of Hamburg">University of Hamburg</a> (Universität Hamburg) with the University Medical Centre of Hamburg-Eppendorf, the <a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Musik_und_Theater_Hamburg" title="Hochschule für Musik und Theater Hamburg">University of Music and Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Hamburg University of Applied Sciences">Hamburg University of Applied Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/HafenCity_University_Hamburg" title="HafenCity University Hamburg">HafenCity University Hamburg</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Hamburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical University of Hamburg">Hamburg University of Technology</a>. Seven universities are private, like the <a href="/wiki/Bucerius_Law_School" title="Bucerius Law School">Bucerius Law School</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_School_of_Business_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamburg School of Business Administration">Hamburg School of Business Administration</a>. The city has also smaller private colleges and universities, including many religious and special-purpose institutions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Schmidt_University" title="Helmut Schmidt University">Helmut Schmidt University</a> (formerly the University of the Federal Armed Forces Hamburg).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> Hamburg is home to one of the oldest international schools in Germany, the <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Hamburg" title="International School of Hamburg">International School of Hamburg</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hamburg has nine <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twin towns and sister cities</a> around the world. <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> became its newest sister city in 2010.<span class="languageicon">(in German)</span><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr valign="top">
<td>
<ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People_from_Hamburg">People from Hamburg</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hamburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: People from Hamburg">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Hamburg" title="Category:People from Hamburg">Category:People from Hamburg</a></div>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>In Hamburg it's hard to find a native Hamburger. A hurried and superficial search turns up only crayfish, people from Pinneberg, and those from Bergedorf. One accompanies the contented little kippers of a striving society; mackerels from Stade, sole from Finkenwerder, herrings from Cuxhaven swim in expectant throngs through the streets of my city and lobsters patrol the stock exchange with open claws.... The first so-called unguarded glance always lands on the bottom of the sea and falls into twilight of the aquarium. <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Heine" title="Heinrich Heine">Heinrich Heine</a> must have had the same experience when he tried, with his cultivated scorn and gifted melancholy, to find the people of Hamburg.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/Siegfried_Lenz" title="Siegfried Lenz">Siegfried Lenz</a>, in <i>Leute von Hamburg</i> (People of Hamburg) <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-423-11538-4" title="Special:BookSources/978-3-423-11538-4">978-3-423-11538-4</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>

<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFBausch2007" class="citation">Bausch, Karl-Heinz (2007), "Die deutsche Sprache—eine Dialektlandschaft", <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110719043439/http://www.ifl-nationalatlas.de/download/bsppdf/Band_6_bsp.pdf"><i>Nationalatlas Bundesrepublik Deutschland</i></a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span> (in German), Leipzig: Leibniz-Institut für Länderkunde, pp.&#160;94–95, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3-8274-0947-0" title="Special:BookSources/3-8274-0947-0">3-8274-0947-0</a>, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ifl-nationalatlas.de/download/bsppdf/Band_6_bsp.pdf">the original</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span> on 19 July 2011<span class="reference-accessdate">, retrieved <span class="nowrap">24 September</span> 2008</span></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHamburg&amp;rft.atitle=Die+deutsche+Sprache%E2%80%94eine+Dialektlandschaft&amp;rft.aufirst=Karl-Heinz&amp;rft.aulast=Bausch&amp;rft.btitle=Nationalatlas+Bundesrepublik+Deutschland&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.isbn=3-8274-0947-0&amp;rft.pages=94-95&amp;rft.place=Leipzig&amp;rft.pub=Leibniz-Institut+f%C3%BCr+L%C3%A4nderkunde&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ifl-nationalatlas.de%2Fdownload%2Fbsppdf%2FBand_6_bsp.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several places are named ...brook (Billbrook, Brooktor, Grasbrook, Hammerbrook, Hellbrook, Iserbrook) rather than Standard German ...bruch (neutr.; =brook riverscape), Bullenhusen rather than Bullenhausen, Lohbrügge rather than Lohbrücke, several localities starting with Nien... (Niendorf, Nienstedten) rather than Neuen..., or ending ...hude (Dockenhuden, Harvestehude, Winterhude) rather than ...hut[ung] (fem.; =pasture), Uhlenhorst rather than Eulenhorst, several places and water bodies are named ...bek (Barmbek, Eilbek, Fischbek, Flottbek, Goldbek, Isebek, Kirchsteinbek, Langenbek, Osterbek, Pepermölenbek, Wandsbek) rather than ...bach, several places and water bodies are called ...fleet (Alsterfleet, Bleichenfleet, Moorfleet) rather than ...fließ (=brook, stream). Further toponyms with no close Standard German correspondents appear, such as ...büttel (=inhabited place; Eimsbüttel, Fuhlsbüttel, Hummelsbüttel, Poppenbüttel, Wellingsbüttel) or Twiete (=alley wedged between buildings). Like in other parts of Northern Germany ...stedt (Bergstedt, Billstedt, Duvenstedt, Eidelstedt, Lokstedt, Mellingstedt, Nienstedten, Ohlstedt, Rahlstedt) prevails over ...stadt (=town, originally simply stead).</span></li>

<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a> were both capital of the Westphalian Quarter at different times.</li>
<li><sup><small>2</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> gained importance once <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> became inaccessible due to the silting of the <a href="/wiki/Zwin" title="Zwin">Zwin</a> channel.</li>
</ul>
